The Rational Proof for Predestination
The author deduces fixed predestination from the nature of truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that all future events are determined, based on the impossibility of altering the truth value of a past statement.

Core Idea
The impossibility of retroactively altering truth proves that future events are fixed.

In this passage, the author presents a logical demonstration that all future events are predetermined. He begins by noting that among two contradictory statements about a future event, one must be genuinely true in reality. He then shows that if that true statement could fail to occur, it would require a change in the past, which is impossible. This leads to the conclusion that what is truly predicted must necessarily occur.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the logical structure.
The author uses a reductio ad absurdum argument.
2
Identify the key claim
The author asserts that for any pair of contradictory statements about a future event, one is true in reality. Why is this important for predestination?
This sets up the proof.
3
Follow the proof step-by-step
Trace the hypothetical: suppose the true statement (event will occur at time T) does not occur. What follows? The statement becomes false from its inception, which means its truth value changes retroactively—an impossibility.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since the non-occurrence leads to impossibility, it is impossible. Therefore, the occurrence is necessary. This shows that future events are fixed and predetermined.
This aligns with the doctrine of qadr.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this proof does and does not establish. It does not rely on knowledge of which event is true, only that truth itself requires determinism.
This addresses a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إحدى هاتين القضيتين هي الموصوفة بالصدقية في نفس الأمر ، والأخرى هي الموصوفة بالكذبية في نفس الأمر بل نحن لا نعرف أن الموصوف بالصدقية أي الطرفين ؟ والموصوف بالكذبية أيهما ؟ فأما في نفس الأمر ، فإنه يجب أن يكون أحدهما بعينه موصوفاً بالصدقية ، والأخرى بالكذبية . إذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : إن هذا يقتضي أن تكون جميع الحوادث المستقبلة : مقدرة على وجه ، يمتنع تطرق الزيادة والنقصان والتغيير إليها . على ما هو مذهبنا في مسألة القضاء والقدر . والدليل عليه : أن الجانب الذي صدق عليه أنه سيقع في الوقت الفلاني . إما أن يكون أن لا يقع في ذلك الوقت ، أو لا عكس . والأول باطل . لأن كل ما كان [ ممكناً (۱) ] فإنه لا يلزم من فرض وقوعـه محـال . فليفرض غير واقع . وإذا لم يقع ، صار قولنا : إنه سيقع : كذباً من أول وقت دخول هذا الخبر في الوجود . وكنا قد فرضنا : أنه كان موصوفاً بالصدقية . فإذا لم يحصل ذلك الفعل ، في ذلك الوقت ، لزم من عدم وقوعه في ذلك الوقت ، ارتفاع الصدقية من ذلك الخبر ، من أول دخوله في الوجود . فيلزم أن يكون عدم وقوع ذلك الفعل في ذلك الوقت ، موجباً زوال صفة الصدقية عنه في الزمان الماضي ، فيفضي هذا إلى إيقاع التصرف في الزمان الماضي . وإنه محال . فثبت : أن عدم وقوع ذلك الفعل في ذلك الوقت ، يلزم منه محال . والممكن هو الذي لا يلزم من فرض وقوعه محال . فثبت : أن عدم وقوعه في ذلك الوقت محال . فكان وقوعه فيه واجباً وهو المطلوب .
One of these two propositions is described as true in reality, and the other is described as false in reality. But we do not know which of the two sides is described as true and which is described as false. So in reality, it is necessary that one specific one be described as true and the other as false. If this is established, we say: This requires that all future events be determined in such a way that no increase, decrease, or change can occur to them, according to our doctrine in the matter of predestination (al-qaḍāʾ wa al-qadar). The proof for it: The side that it is true that it will occur at a certain time—either it is that it will not occur at that time, or not. The first is false. Because everything that is possible, it is not necessary from supposing its occurrence that an impossibility follows. So let it be supposed as not occurring. And if it does not occur, our statement 'it will occur' becomes false from the first moment this report came into existence. And we had supposed that it was described as true. So if that action does not occur at that time, from its non-occurrence at that time follows the removal of truthfulness from that report from the first moment of its existence. So it would follow that the non-occurrence of that action at that time necessitates the removal of the attribute of truthfulness from it in past time, leading to affecting the past, and this is impossible. So it is established that non-occurrence of that action at that time entails an impossibility. The possible is that from supposing which no impossibility follows. So it is established that its non-occurrence at that time is impossible. So its occurrence at that time is necessary, which is what was sought.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for predestination. The author first establishes that among two contradictory statements about a future event, one is true in reality. He then argues that this requires all future events to be fixed and unchangeable. The proof is: Suppose the true statement is that an event will occur at a specific time. If that event does not occur, the statement becomes false from its very inception (since it was claimed to be true). This would mean that the non-occurrence retroactively changes the truth value of the past statement, which is impossible. Therefore, the non-occurrence is impossible, and the occurrence is necessary. Thus, future events are determined.

Correction: The proof only requires that there is a truth of the matter, not that we know it.

Key Takeaway
The necessary truth of one of two contradictory future statements entails that the truly predicted event must occur, proving that all future events are predetermined.

The First Aspect: Truth and Falsehood Require a Subject
Al-Razi presents the first aspect of his response, establishing that truth and falsehood require a subject.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's first argument that every statement must have a determinate truth-value because truth and falsehood are opposites requiring a subject.

Core Idea
Truth and falsehood are real attributes that require a subject, so every statement is either true or false.

Al-Razi begins his refutation by laying down the logical foundation: truth and falsehood are contradictory qualities. If a statement is not true, it must be false, and vice versa. This means that every statement necessarily possesses one of these attributes. He then addresses a potential objection that these attributes might be merely negative, showing that even negative attributes require a specific substrate.

Guided Path
1
Read the first aspect passage
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning of the answer through the end of the first aspect. Focus on how Al-Razi establishes the necessity of a determinate truth-value.
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
The first part sets up the opposition between truth and falsehood. The second part rebuts the claim that they are merely negative attributes. Notice how Al-Razi argues that even a negative attribute needs a subject.
3
Reflect on the objection
Why might someone think truth and falsehood are negative? Al-Razi counters by showing that any negation must be of something from something that is apt to have it, which requires a specific subject.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب من وجوه :
الأول : إن الصدقية والكذبية متقابلان بالسلب والإيجاب . لأن الصدق هو الخبر المطابق ، والكذب هو الخبر الذي لا يطابق . ولما كان هذان الوصفان متقابلين بالسلب والإيجاب ، كان أحدهما لا محالة صفة ثابتة موجودة . وإذا كان كذلك ، وجب أن يحصل له موصوف معين . وحينئذ يحصل المطلوب .
ولا ينافي مذهبنا أن الصدقية والكذبية وصفان سلبيان ، لأن الوصف السلبي لا بد له أيضاً من محل معين . لأن هذا السلب عبارة عن عدم شيء عن شيء من شأنه أن يكون حاصلاً له فيما لم يحصل إمكان حصول ذلك الوصف لذلك الموصوف ، امتنع أن يحكم الذهن بزواله عنه . فثبت : أنه وإن كان سلبياً إلا أنه لا بد له من محل معين .
الثاني : وهو إنه إذا كان هذا الطرف بعينه خالياً عن الصدقية والكذبية ، كان مجرد قولنا : « زيد غدا يمشي ) : خالياً عن كونه كاذباً ، وخالياً عن كونه صادقاً . فتكون هذه القضية بعينها خالية عن النقيضين معاً . وذلك محال ، وكذا القول في الطرف الآخر. لا يقال : إنه وإن خلا عن الصدقية بعينها ، والكذبية بعينها ، لكنه ما خلا عن كونه . إما صدقاً وإما كذبا . لأنا نقول : هذا الإيهام إنما يقع في الأذهان. أما في الأعيان . فالحاصل أما وصف الصدقية ، وإما وصف الكذبية. فإذا كانت القضية خالية عنهما معاً ، لزم خلوهما عن النقيضين ، وهو محال .
واعلم : أن هذا البرهان قد دل على أن جميع الحوادث المستقبلة ، مترتبة في أنفسها ترتباً ، يمتنع على المتقدم أن يصير متأخراً ، أو على المتأخر أن يصير متقدماً . وذلك يبطل الاعتزال بالكلية . ثم إنا إذا أردنا أن نبين أن ذلك الوجوب إنما حصل بإيجاب الله تعالى وبتقديره . قلنا : إن ذلك الموجب يمتنع أن يكون بالذات . لما ثبت : أن الممكن لذاته ، لا يكون واجباً لذاته . بل لا بد وأن يكون واجباً بالغير . وذلك الغير ليس هو العبد . لأن هذا الوجوب حاصل قبل قصد العبد إلى إيجاده ، بل حاصل قبل وجود العبد . وكيف . وهذا الوجوب الذي قررناه كان حاصلا من الأزل إلى الأبد . ولا بد وأن يكون المقتضى لذلك الوجوب أمراً كان مستمراً من الأزل ، وما ذاك إلا الله سبحانه . فثبت : أن هذا الوجوب إنما حصل في هذه الحوادث المستقبلة ، بتقدير الله وبإيجاده إما ابتداء وإما بواسطة . وذلك هو المطلوب .
وهذا برهان شريف ، لا بد من التأمل فيه، لحيصل الوقوف عليه ، كما ينبغي .
وبالله التوفيق
The answer is from several aspects:
First: Trutiness and falseness are opposites by negation and affirmation. Because truth is the report that corresponds, and falsehood is the report that does not correspond. And since these two attributes are opposites by negation and affirmation, one of them necessarily is a fixed existing attribute. And if that is so, then it must have a specific subject. And then the desired is obtained.
And it does not contradict our position that trutiness and falseness are negative attributes, because the negative attribute also necessarily has a specific substrate. Because this negation is the non-existence of something from something that is apt to have it. If it is not possible for that attribute to belong to that subject, the mind cannot judge its removal from it. So it is established that even though it is negative, it necessarily has a specific substrate.
Second: And that if this specific statement is free from trutiness and falseness, then our mere saying 'Zayd will walk tomorrow' would be free from being false and free from being true. So this very proposition would be free from both contradictories together. And that is impossible, and likewise for the other statement. It cannot be said: 'Even if it is free from trutiness itself and falseness itself, it is not free from being either true or false.' For we say: This illusion occurs only in minds. As for actual reality, what obtains is either the attribute of truth or the attribute of falsehood. So if the proposition is free from both together, it would be free from the two contradictories, which is impossible.
And know: This proof has indicated that all future events are ordered in themselves in an order such that the earlier cannot become later, nor the later become earlier. And that invalidates Mu'tazilism entirely. Then, if we wish to show that that necessity came about by the command of God Almighty and His decree, we say: That necessitator cannot be essential. Because it is established that the possible in itself cannot be necessary in itself. Rather, it must be necessary through another. And that other is not the servant. Because this necessity exists before the servant's intention to bring it about, rather it exists before the existence of the servant. How? And this necessity which we have established has been occurring from eternity to eternity. And the requirer of that necessity must be something that has been continuous from eternity, and that is none other than God, may He be exalted. So it is established that this necessity occurred in these future events only by God's decree and His bringing into existence, either directly or through an intermediary. And that is what was sought.
And this is a noble proof, which must be pondered so that one may grasp it as it deserves.
And with God is success.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents Al-Razi's response to an objection concerning the truth-value of future contingent statements. It is a combination of a refutation and a proof. The author begins by enumerating two aspects (وجوه) of the answer.

The first aspect: Truth (صدقية) and falsehood (كذبية) are opposites by negation and affirmation, meaning one is the negation of the other. Truth is correspondence, falsehood is lack thereof. Since they are opposites, one of them must actually be a fixed attribute of any subject. This requires a determinate subject (موصوف معين). Thus, every statement has a determinate truth-value. The author then addresses a potential conflict with the view that truth and falsehood are negative attributes. He argues that even a negative attribute requires a specific substrate (محل معين) because negation is the absence of something from something apt to have it. Without the possibility of that attribute, the mind cannot judge its removal. So a determinate subject is needed.

The second aspect: If a statement like 'Zayd will walk tomorrow' were free from both truth and falsehood, it would be free from both contradictories simultaneously, which is impossible. The objection that it could be 'either true or false' as a mental consideration is rejected; in actual reality, it must have one or the other. Therefore, future statements have determinate truth-values.

The author then draws a key theological conclusion: this proof entails that all future events are rigidly ordered in themselves, invalidating the Mu'tazilite position. To further demonstrate that this necessity is from God, he argues that the necessitator (موجب) cannot be essential (بالذات) because the possible cannot be necessary by itself. It must be necessary through another (بالغير). That other is not the servant, as the necessity exists before the servant's intention or even existence. The only being continuous from eternity is God. Thus, the necessity in future events is by God's decree and causation, directly or indirectly. The author concludes that this is a noble proof requiring careful reflection.

Key Terms
الصدقية
الكذبية
السلب والإيجاب
الموصوف
المحل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that truth and falsehood are merely mental concepts that can be applied arbitrarily.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that they are real attributes that necessarily adhere to a subject, whether positive or negative, requiring a specific proposition.

Checkpoint
According to the first aspect, what is the relationship between truth and falsehood?
A) They are unrelated.
B) They are opposites by negation and affirmation.
C) They are both negative attributes.
D) They require no subject.

Key Takeaway
Every statement must have a determinate truth-value because truth and falsehood are opposites that require a specific subject.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every statement you utter is either true or false in God's sight, even before you speak it, how does that change the weight you give to your words? Will you begin to treat every claim you make as if it were literally recorded in a ledger of truth?
?
Al-Razi argues that even negative attributes (like 'I am not worthy') require a real subject. Where in your life do you use negative statements to define yourself or others? How might you begin to replace those with truth that reflects your fixed reality as God's creation?
?
If truth is a real attribute that cannot be suspended, then the truth of Allah's revelation is absolute. What is one area of your life where you have been treating divine truth as optional or negotiable? What concrete step will you take today to submit to that truth?

Divine Decree
intermediate
5 min
The Second Aspect: The Impossibility of a Proposition Free from Both Truth and Falsehood
Al-Razi presents the second aspect, showing that a proposition cannot lack both truth and falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's second argument that a proposition cannot be free from both truth and falsehood, as that would violate the law of excluded middle.

Core Idea
A proposition cannot be neither true nor false; that would free it from both contradictories, which is impossible.

In his second aspect, Al-Razi uses a direct logical argument: if a future statement like 'Zayd will walk tomorrow' were neither true nor false, it would be free from both contradictories simultaneously. He then refutes a possible objection that it could be considered 'either true or false' in the mind, insisting that in reality it must be one or the other.

Guided Path
1
Read the second aspect passage
Read from 'الثاني' to the end of the paragraph. Pay attention to the conditional and the conclusion.
2
Understand the logical impossibility
The argument is that if a proposition is free from both truth and falsehood, it is free from both contradictories, which is impossible because every proposition must be either true or false.
This is the law of excluded middle.
3
Evaluate the objection and reply
The objection says the proposition might be considered 'either true or false' as a mental possibility. Al-Razi replies that in actual reality, the attribute is either truth or falsehood, not a mental consideration.

Source Text

Commentary

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi argue would happen if a statement were free from both truth and falsehood?
A) It would be a valid middle state.
B) It would be free from both contradictories, which is impossible.
C) It would be considered true in the mind.
D) It would be neither true nor false in the mind only.

Key Takeaway
A proposition cannot be free from both truth and falsehood because that would violate the law of excluded middle; it must be either true or false in reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your future—tomorrow, next year—do you live as if God has already determined every detail with certainty, or do you mentally treat some outcomes as 'undecided'? Where does your heart truly rest?
?
Al-Razi argues that a statement about the future is already true or false in reality, not merely in possibility. How does this truth confront your tendency to procrastinate or to hope without action? What would change if you truly believed that every future event is already fixed in God's decree?
?
You may claim to believe in qadr, but your anxiety about tomorrow reveals a hidden assumption: that the future is open and undetermined. Will you repent from this subtle disbelief and submit your whole future to the One who knows all?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
The Grand Conclusion: Future Events Are Fixed by Divine Decree
Al-Razi concludes that future events are ordered and necessitated by God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi's arguments about truth-value lead to the conclusion that all future events are necessary by God's decree, refuting Mu'tazilism.

Core Idea
The determinate truth of future statements implies a fixed order that can only come from God's eternal decree.

After presenting two logical arguments for the determinacy of future statements, Al-Razi now draws the theological conclusion: all future events are ordered in themselves such that the earlier cannot become later, which completely invalidates the Mu'tazilite position. He then argues that this necessity is not self-caused but must come from God, as it exists before the servant's existence and intention.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding passage
Read from 'واعلم' to the end. Notice how Al-Razi moves from logical argument to theological conclusion.
2
Understand the refutation of Mu'tazilism
Al-Razi claims that his proof shows that future events are ordered, making any change impossible. This contradicts the Mu'tazilite view that human actions are not predetermined.
3
Trace the argument for divine causality
The necessity cannot come from the essence of the event (since it is possible), nor from the servant (since it exists before the servant). It must come from God, the eternal being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And since these two attributes are opposites by negation and affirmation, one of them necessarily is a fixed existing attribute. And if that is so, then it must have a specific subject. And then the desired is obtained.
And it does not contradict our position that trutiness and falseness are negative attributes, because the negative attribute also necessarily has a specific substrate. Because this negation is the non-existence of something from something that is apt to have it. If it is not possible for that attribute to belong to that subject, the mind cannot judge its removal from it. So it is established that even though it is negative, it necessarily has a specific substrate.

So this very proposition would be free from both contradictories together. And that is impossible, and likewise for the other statement. As for actual reality, what obtains is either the attribute of truth or the attribute of falsehood. So if the proposition is free from both together, it would be free from the two contradictories, which is impossible.
And know: This proof has indicated that all future events are ordered in themselves in an order such that the earlier cannot become later, nor the later become earlier. And that invalidates Mu'tazilism entirely. Then, if we wish to show that that necessity came about by the command of God Almighty and His decree, we say: That necessitator cannot be essential. Because it is established that the possible in itself cannot be necessary in itself. Rather, it must be necessary through another. And that other is not the servant. Because this necessity exists before the servant's intention to bring it about, rather it exists before the existence of the servant. How? And this necessity which we have established has been occurring from eternity to eternity. And the requirer of that necessity must be something that has been continuous from eternity, and that is none other than God, may He be exalted. So it is established that this necessity occurred in these future events only by God's decree and His bringing into existence, either directly or through an intermediary. And that is what was sought.
And this is a noble proof, which must be pondered so that one may grasp it as it deserves.
And with God is success.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents Al-Razi's response to an objection concerning the truth-value of future contingent statements. It is a combination of a refutation and a proof. The author begins by enumerating two aspects (وجوه) of the answer.

The first aspect: Truth (صدقية) and falsehood (كذبية) are opposites by negation and affirmation, meaning one is the negation of the other. Truth is correspondence, falsehood is lack thereof. Since they are opposites, one of them must actually be a fixed attribute of any subject. This requires a determinate subject (موصوف معين). Thus, every statement has a determinate truth-value. The author then addresses a potential conflict with the view that truth and falsehood are negative attributes. He argues that even a negative attribute requires a specific substrate (محل معين) because negation is the absence of something from something apt to have it. Without the possibility of that attribute, the mind cannot judge its removal. So a determinate subject is needed.

The second aspect: If a statement like 'Zayd will walk tomorrow' were free from both truth and falsehood, it would be free from both contradictories simultaneously, which is impossible. The objection that it could be 'either true or false' as a mental consideration is rejected; in actual reality, it must have one or the other. Therefore, future statements have determinate truth-values.

The author then draws a key theological conclusion: this proof entails that all future events are rigidly ordered in themselves, invalidating the Mu'tazilite position. To further demonstrate that this necessity is from God, he argues that the necessitator (موجب) cannot be essential (بالذات) because the possible cannot be necessary by itself. It must be necessary through another (بالغير). That other is not the servant, as the necessity exists before the servant's intention or even existence. The only being continuous from eternity is God. Thus, the necessity in future events is by God's decree and causation, directly or indirectly. The author concludes that this is a noble proof requiring careful reflection.

Key Terms
الحوادث المستقبلة
الوجوب
المقتضى
الاعتزال
تقدير الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Mu'tazilites believe that human actions are not predetermined and that future events have no fixed truth-values before they occur.
Correction: Al-Razi's argument shows that future events have determinate truth-values and are ordered, which necessitates divine predestination.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Razi, why does the necessity of future events not come from the servant?
A) Because the servant has free will.
B) Because the necessity exists before the servant's existence.
C) Because the servant cannot create necessity.
D) Because the servant is not eternal.

Key Takeaway
All future events are fixed by God's decree, as their determinate truth requires a necessary order that only God can provide.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If all future events are already fixed by God's decree before you were born, does your daily worry about outcomes make sense? What would it look like to truly trust that God's decree is both necessary and good?
?
Al-Razi argues that the necessity of events does not come from your intentions—it exists even before you intend. Does that reality humble you or frighten you? How should it change the way you approach your plans for tomorrow?
?
The proof ends with the claim that only God is eternal and the source of all necessity. Do you live as if that is true, or do you act as if your own efforts are the ultimate cause of your success? What is one specific area where you need to surrender control to God today?

The Seventh Proof: From Divine Foreknowledge to Determinism
Al-Razi presents the seventh proof: divine knowledge necessitates actions, and this necessity is caused by God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi argues that God's exhaustive and infallible knowledge of human actions logically necessitates divine determinism.

Core Idea
God's certain knowledge makes human actions necessary.

Al-Razi now deploys a concise logical proof that links God's knowledge directly to the necessity of actions. If God knows something will occur, it cannot fail to occur. But what grounds that necessity? The proof pushes us to conclude that God Himself must be the ultimate cause, either by choosing to create the action or by creating its preconditions. This passage is a classic example of Ash'arite reasoning against free will.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic text once without worrying about full understanding. Notice the rhythm and key terms like 'معلومة الوقوع' and 'واجب الوقوع'.
The text cuts off at the end; the core argument is still complete.
2
Identify the premises
Find the two premises: 1) God knows whether an action will occur or not. 2) If He knows it will occur, it is necessary; if not, its non-occurrence is necessary.
These are stated in the first two lines.
3
Analyze the conclusion
Al-Razi then concludes that this necessity must come from God, either by direct preference or by creating what necessitates the action. Understand why this follows from the premises.
He offers two possibilities—both trace the necessity back to God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان السابع
أفعال العباد معلومة الوقوع لله تعالى . أو معلومة اللا وقوع . وكل ما هو معلوم الوقوع ، كان واجب الوقوع . وكل ما هو معلوم اللا وقوع ، كان واجب اللا وقوع . وكل ذلك قد تقدم تقريره .
فنقول : ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، وجب أن يكون ذلك الوجوب إما بسبب : أن الله رجع وجودها على عدمها وإما بسبب أن الله تعالى خلق ما يوجب وقوعها ، إما بواسطة ، أو بغير واسطة . وعلى كل هذه التقديرات ، فمقصودنا حاصل .
والذي يدل على صحة هذه المقدمة : أن فعل العبد لما كان واجب
The seventh proof:
The actions of servants are known to occur by God Almighty, or known not to occur. And everything whose occurrence is known is necessary of occurrence. And everything whose non-occurrence is known is necessary of non-occurrence. And all that has been established earlier.
So we say: And whenever the matter is thus, then that necessity must be either because God preferred their existence over their non-existence, or because God Almighty created what necessitates their occurrence, either through an intermediary or without an intermediary. And in all these cases, our goal is attained.
And what indicates the correctness of this premise: that the act of the servant, when it is necessary...
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage introduces the seventh proof (البرهان السابع) concerning divine foreknowledge and determinism. It is a structured argument in the form of a proof.

The author states the premises: All human actions are known by God either to occur or not to occur. Whatever God knows will occur is necessarily occurring; whatever He knows will not occur is necessarily not occurring. These premises are said to have been established earlier (قد تقدم تقريره).

From this, the author concludes that the necessity (الوجوب) of an action's occurrence or non-occurrence must be due to one of two reasons: either (1) God preferred its existence over non-existence, or (2) God created something that necessitates its occurrence, whether directly or through an intermediary. In both cases, the required conclusion (that all actions are determined by God) is achieved.

The author then begins to justify the premise that the act of the servant, when it is necessary [...] but the text cuts off at the end of the page. The fragment suggests he is about to argue that the necessity of the act implies divine causation. Despite incompleteness, the core of the proof is clear: God's exhaustive and infallible knowledge necessitates the predetermined nature of all actions, which is the Ash'arite position against free will.

معلومة الوقوع
واجب الوقوع
الوجوب
رجع وجودها على عدمها
واسطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's knowledge of human actions is passive and does not affect their occurrence.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that God's knowledge entails necessity: if God knows a thing will occur, it must occur, and that necessity itself must be caused by God.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh proof, why is a servant's action necessarily occurring?
A) Because the servant freely chooses it.
B) Because God knows it will occur, and this knowledge makes it necessary.
C) Because the action is possible in itself.
D) Because the servant creates his own action.

Key Takeaway
God's certain knowledge of human actions logically necessitates their occurrence, and this necessity is ultimately caused by God Himself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action you have ever done—even the sins you regret—was known by God from eternity and made necessary by His knowledge? How does that sit with your sense of personal guilt and responsibility?
?
If your actions are ultimately caused by God's decree or His creation of causes, can you still accept that you are genuinely accountable for them? Where do you draw the line between divine determination and your own choice?
?
This proof leaves no room for chance or accident. Are you willing to surrender the idea that any part of your life is outside God's control, even the parts you wish you could change on your own?

Sixth Proof: Necessity of Future Events from God's Predestination
The author presents the sixth proof that future events are necessitated by God's eternal decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof that future events are necessitated by God's eternal decree, and why the necessitating cause cannot be the human will.

Core Idea
The possibility of future events requires an eternal cause: God alone.

This passage presents the sixth proof from the author's treatise, arguing that all future events are necessitated by God's predestination. The proof builds on the principle that possible things require an external necessary cause, and it eliminates the human will as that cause. Let's examine the logical steps carefully.

Guided Path
1
Understand the foundational principle
Begin by grasping the principle that a possible being (الممكن لذاته) cannot be necessary by itself; it must become necessary through another (بالغير). This is the starting point of the proof.
2
Recognize why human will is not the cause
Consider why the human servant cannot be the necessitating cause: the necessity exists before the servant intends the action and even before the servant exists. Therefore, the cause must be something else.
3
Grasp the eternity of the necessity
Notice that the necessity in question is eternal—from pre-eternity to perpetuity. This means its cause must also be eternal.
4
Conclude that God is the cause
Since only God is eternal and independent, the cause must be God. Thus, future events are necessitated by God's predetermination and bringing into existence, either directly or through intermediaries.
5
Reflect on the proof's significance
The author calls this a noble proof that requires deep reflection. Consider how it establishes tawhid in action and refutes attributing ultimate causality to creatures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يكون بالذات . لما ثبت : أن الممكن لذاته ، لا يكون واجباً لذاته . بل لا بد وأن يكون واجباً بالغير . وذلك الغير ليس هو العبد . لأن هذا الوجوب حاصل قبل قصد العبد إلى إيجاده ، بل حاصل قبل وجود العبد . وكيف . وهذا الوجوب الذي قررناه كان حاصلا من الأزل إلى الأبد . ولا بد وأن يكون المقتضى لذلك الوجوب أمراً كان مستمراً من الأزل ، وما ذاك إلا الله سبحانه . فثبت : أن هذا الوجوب إنما حصل في هذه الحوادث المستقبلة ، بتقدير الله وبإيجاده إما ابتداء وإما بواسطة . وذلك هو المطلوب . وهذا برهان شريف ، لا بد من التأمل فيه ، لحيصل الوقوف عليه ، كما ينبغي . وبالله التوفيق
It is by essence. Since it is established that the possible in itself is not necessary in itself. Rather, it must be necessary by another. And that other is not the servant. Because this necessity occurs before the servant's intention to bring it into existence, rather it occurs before the existence of the servant. And how? And this necessity which we have stated was occurring from eternity to eternity. And there must be a cause for that necessity that was continuous from eternity, and that is none other than God, exalted is He. So it is established that this necessity occurs in these future events only by God's predetermination and His bringing into existence, either directly or through an intermediary. And that is what is sought. And this is a noble proof; it must be pondered upon, so that one may grasp it as it deserves. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof (البرهان السادس) for the predestination of future events. The author begins by stating a fundamental principle: a possible entity (الممكن) cannot be necessary by itself (لذاته); it must become necessary through another (بالغير). He then argues that this necessitating other cannot be the human servant (العبد) because the necessity in question exists even before the servant intends the action, indeed before the servant himself exists. The necessity is eternal, from pre-eternity (الأزل) to perpetuity. Therefore, the only possible cause for this eternal necessity is a cause that is itself eternal, which is none other than God. The conclusion is that the necessity of future events comes from God's predetermination (تقدير) and His bringing into existence (إيجاد), either directly or through intermediaries. The author then remarks that this proof is noble and requires careful reflection.

Key Terms

الممكن لذاته
تقدير الله
الإيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The necessity of future events comes from the human will.
Correction: The proof shows that this necessity exists before the human will and even before the human's existence, so it cannot originate from the human.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth proof, why cannot the necessitating cause of future events be the human servant?
A) Because the human will is not eternal.
B) Because the necessity exists before the human intends or even exists.
C) Because the human is a possible being.
D) Because God's predetermination is more powerful.

Key Takeaway
The sixth proof demonstrates that the necessity of future events originates solely from God's eternal decree, not from human will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about a specific future event you are anxious about planning for. Does this proof that its necessity is from God before you even intend it bring you peace or resistance? What does your reaction reveal about what you truly believe is in control?
?
When you succeed or fail, do you attribute the outcome to your own skill or effort as the real cause? How would your heart and actions change if you fully internalized that even the possibility of your effort itself is necessitated by God's eternal decree?
?
This proof strips away any sense of self-sufficiency. In what area of your life are you still acting as if your own will is the ultimate decider? What would be one concrete step to surrender that area to God's predestination today?

The Seventh Proof: Premise of Divine Knowledge and Necessity
Opening premise and two cause possibilities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial premise of the seventh proof: that God's knowledge of human actions implies their necessity, and that this necessity must have a cause.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge necessitates actions, but the cause is separate.

The author begins the seventh proof with a fundamental premise: God knows all human actions as either occurring or not occurring. Whatever He knows will occur is necessary to occur. This necessity cannot be without a cause, so the author identifies two possible causes: God's preference or His creation of necessitating factors. This lesson lays the groundwork for the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening premise
Read the Arabic passage that states God knows all human actions and that known actions are necessary.
Notice the author uses 'known to occur' and 'known not to occur' as comprehensive categories.
2
Identify the two possible causes
The passage says the necessity must be due to either God's preference or His creation of what necessitates the action.
The word 'رجع' is corrected to 'رجح' meaning to prefer.
3
Reflect on why necessity requires a cause
Consider why the author insists that necessity cannot be without a cause—this is a key principle in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان السابع
أفعال العباد معلومة الوقوع لله تعالى . أو معلومة اللا وقوع . وكل ما هو معلوم الوقوع ، كان واجب الوقوع . وكل ما هو معلوم اللا وقوع ، كان واجب اللا وقوع . وكل ذلك قد تقدم تقريره . فنقول : ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، وجب أن يكون ذلك الوجوب إما بسبب : أن الله رجع وجودها على عدمها وإما بسبب أن الله تعالى خلق ما يوجب وقوعها ، إما بواسطة ، أو بغير واسطة . وعلى كل هذه التقديرات ، فمقصودنا حاصل . والذي يدل على صحة هذه المقدمة : أن فعل العبد لما كان واجب الوقوع في ذلك الوقت المعين. فإما أن يكون وجوبه لذاته . وهو محال . لأن الممكن لذاته ، لا يكون واجباً لذاته. وإما أن يكون وجوبه لغيره وذلك الغير . إما العبد ، وإما الله . والأول باطل . لأن الفعل الذي علم الله وقوعه في الوقت الفلاني محكوم عليه في الأزل بأنه واجب أن يقع في الوقت الفلاني فلا يزال . فالوجوب بهذا التفسير حاصل في الأزل ، بما لا يكون حاصلاً في الأزل : محال . ولما بطل هذا ، ثبت : أن المؤثر في حصول الوجوب بالتفسير الذي ذكرناه : صفة من صفات الله تعالى . وتلك الصفة . إما العلم ، وإما غيره . والأول باطل . لأن العلم يتعلق بالمعلوم على ما هو عليه ، وهو يتبع المعلوم ولا يستتبعه . فيمتنع أن يكون المقتضي لهذا الوجوب هو علم الله . فثبت : أن المقتضي لهذا الوجوب : صفة من صفات الله ، باشرها في ترجيح أحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر ، وتلك الصفة ليست إلا القدرة أو الإرادة . فثبت : أن المؤثر في وقوع أفعال العباد ، ليس إلا قدرة الله إما ابتداء أو بواسطة . وذلك هو المطلوب . وهذا أيضاً برهان شريف المطلوب . إلا أن البرهان المبني على اعتبار أحوال المتناقضين أشرف من هذا البرهان . وذلك لأنا في هذا البرهان نفتقر لإقامة الدلالة على كونه تعالى عالم بجميع المعلومات . حتى يثبت لنا عند ذلك : أنه تعالى كان عالماً بأفعال العباد قبل وقوعها . وهذه المقدمة إن أخذناها على سبيل أن الخصم شاهد عليها ، كان هذا الكلام الزاما برهانياً . فإن حاولنا إثباتها بالدليل ، تعذر ذلك علينا . لأن المعتمد في إثبات أنه تعالى عالم بأفعال العباد قبل وقوعها : هو أنه تعالى مقدر لها وخالق لها . فوجب أن يكون عالماً بها . فنحن إنما أثبتنا كونه تعالى عالماً بها قبل وقوعها ، لأنه ثبت كونه تعالى
The Seventh Proof. Human actions are known to God as occurring or as not occurring. And everything known to occur is necessary to occur. And everything known not to occur is necessary not to occur. And all that has been previously established. So we say: When the matter is thus, then that necessity must be either because God preferred their existence over their non-existence, or because God created what necessitates their occurrence, either directly or without an intermediary. And according to all these estimations, our goal is attained. And that which indicates the soundness of this premise is: Since the servant's action is necessary to occur at that specific time, then either its necessity is due to itself—and that is impossible, because the possible in itself is not necessary in itself—or its necessity is due to something else, and that something else is either the servant or God. The first is false, because the action which God knows will occur at such-and-such a time is judged in pre-eternity as being necessary to occur at that time, so it continues. Thus, the necessity according to this interpretation is realized in pre-eternity, but that which is not realized in pre-eternity is impossible. When this is invalidated, it is established that the effective agent in bringing about the necessity according to the interpretation we have mentioned is an attribute of God. That attribute is either knowledge or something else. The first is false, because knowledge relates to the known as it is, and it follows the known and does not cause it. So it is impossible that the cause of this necessity is God's knowledge. So it is established that the cause of this necessity is an attribute of God that directly tilts one of the two sides of the possible over the other, and that attribute is only power or will. So it is established that the effective agent in the occurrence of human actions is only God's power, either directly or through an intermediary. And that is what is sought. This also is a noble proof of what is sought. However, the proof based on considering the states of two contradictories is more noble than this proof. That is because in this proof we need to establish the evidence that God is knowledgeable of all things, so that we may thereby prove that He was knowledgeable of human actions before their occurrence. If we take this premise as a concession from the opponent, then this statement becomes a dialectical refutation. But if we attempt to prove it by evidence, that becomes difficult for us, because the basis for proving that God is knowledgeable of human actions before their occurrence is that He is their predeterminer and creator; so He must be knowledgeable of them. Thus, we only prove that He is knowledgeable of them before their occurrence because it is established that He is
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof (البرهان السابع) for the predestination of human actions. The author begins by stating a premise: God knows all human actions as either occurring or not occurring. Whatever He knows to occur is necessary to occur, and whatever He knows not to occur is necessary not to occur. This necessity must have a cause. The author then argues that this cause is either God's preference (ارجح? رجع likely means رجح) or His creation of what necessitates the action. The proof then proceeds by examining the nature of the action's necessity: it cannot be necessary by itself (because it is possible), nor can it be necessary by the servant (because the necessity is eternal, predating the servant). Thus, the necessity must come from an attribute of God. The author then eliminates knowledge as the cause, because knowledge follows the known and does not cause it. Therefore, the cause must be either power (القدرة) or will (الإرادة). The conclusion is that God's power is the effective agent in causing human actions, directly or through intermediaries. The author then evaluates this proof compared to another (the proof based on contradictory states), noting that this proof requires first establishing God's knowledge of future actions, which itself depends on His being the creator and predeterminer. If the opponent concedes this knowledge, the proof works as a dialectical argument; otherwise, it is difficult to prove independently. This shows the author's methodological awareness.

Key Terms
معلوم الوقوع
وجوب الوقوع
المقتضي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's knowledge alone forces actions without any other cause.
Correction: The author argues that knowledge alone does not cause; there must be an additional cause such as God's preference or creation.

Checkpoint
Which two possible causes does the author identify for the necessity of human actions?
A) God's power and will
B) God's preference and creation of necessitating factors
C) God's knowledge and will
D) The action's essence and the servant's choice

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge of actions implies their necessity, and that necessity must be caused either by His preference or by His creation of necessitating factors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Every action you have ever done and will ever do is 'known to occur' by God with absolute certainty. Does that knowledge comfort you, or does it unsettle you? Why? Now, read again: that occurrence is necessary—but the necessity has a cause either from God's preference or from what He created. How does this affect the way you understand your own responsibility for your sins? Take a moment to think of one sin you committed. Can you truly say you are accountable if its occurrence was necessary? Let this tension drive you to seek refuge in God's mercy and justice, not to escape blame, but to embrace the mystery of qadar with humility.
?
This proof says that the necessity of your actions is caused either by God's direct preference or by factors He created. Which of these two feels more real to you in your daily life? Do you see your choices as being weighed by God's preference, or do you sense causes around you pushing you to act? Locate one area in your life where you feel you lack control over your actions. According to this passage, what is the ultimate source of that necessity? How does that knowledge change your prayer for change? Commit today to ask God to make the causes He created lead you to what pleases Him.
?
If God's knowledge makes your actions necessary, and that necessity must have a cause from Him, then what room is there for your own will? Yet the author does not deny human actions. Pause and consider: Are you living as if your actions are nothing but divine puppetry, or as if they are entirely your own? Both extremes are off. This passage forces you to confront the middle: a divinely caused necessity that still attributes actions to you. How does that middle ground shape your gratitude for good deeds and your repentance for bad ones? Let it lead you to a deeper trust in God's wisdom and a more sincere striving to obey Him.

Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
The Cause of Necessity: Eliminating Self and Servant, Establishing God's Attribute
Elimination of alternatives to establish divine power as cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the necessity of human actions cannot be due to the action itself or the servant, and must be due to an attribute of God, which is power or will.

Core Idea
The necessity of actions is eternal, so it cannot originate from the temporal servant.

Building on the premise that necessity requires a cause, the author now examines the possible sources of that necessity. He argues it cannot be intrinsic to the action (since it is possible) nor from the servant (since the necessity is eternal), so it must be from God. He then eliminates divine knowledge as a direct cause, concluding that power or will is the effective agent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the options: self, servant, or God
The passage argues that the necessity of the action must be caused either by the action itself, the servant, or God.
2
Eliminate self-necessity
The action is possible in itself, so it cannot be necessary by itself. This is a basic kalam principle.
Possible things are not inherently necessary.
3
Eliminate servant-necessity
The necessity is eternal (judged in pre-eternity), so it cannot be caused by the temporal servant.
The text says the action is 'judged in pre-eternity as necessary'.
4
Eliminate knowledge, leaving power/will
The author shows that knowledge cannot be the cause because it follows the known. The cause must be an attribute that tilts the possible, which is power or will.
This step is crucial: knowledge is not creative, power and will are.

البرهان السابع
أفعال العباد معلومة الوقوع لله تعالى . أو معلومة اللا وقوع . وكل ما هو معلوم الوقوع ، كان واجب الوقوع . وكل ما هو معلوم اللا وقوع ، كان واجب اللا وقوع . وكل ذلك قد تقدم تقريره . فنقول : ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، وجب أن يكون ذلك الوجوب إما بسبب : أن الله رجع وجودها على عدمها وإما بسبب أن الله تعالى خلق ما يوجب وقوعها ، إما بواسطة ، أو بغير واسطة . وعلى كل هذه التقديرات ، فمقصودنا حاصل . والذي يدل على صحة هذه المقدمة : أن فعل العبد لما كان واجب الوقوع في ذلك الوقت المعين. فإما أن يكون وجوبه لذاته . وهو محال . لأن الممكن لذاته ، لا يكون واجباً لذاته. وإما أن يكون وجوبه لغيره وذلك الغير . إما العبد ، وإما الله . والأول باطل . لأن الفعل الذي علم الله وقوعه في الوقت الفلاني محكوم عليه في الأزل بأنه واجب أن يقع في الوقت الفلاني فلا يزال . فالوجوب بهذا التفسير حاصل في الأزل ، بما لا يكون حاصلاً في الأزل : محال . ولما بطل هذا ، ثبت : أن المؤثر في حصول الوجوب بالتفسير الذي ذكرناه : صفة من صفات الله تعالى . وتلك الصفة . إما العلم ، وإما غيره . والأول باطل . لأن العلم يتعلق بالمعلوم على ما هو عليه ، وهو يتبع المعلوم ولا يستتبعه . فيمتنع أن يكون المقتضي لهذا الوجوب هو علم الله . فثبت : أن المقتضي لهذا الوجوب : صفة من صفات الله ، باشرها في ترجيح أحد طرفي الممكن على الآخر ، وتلك الصفة ليست إلا القدرة أو الإرادة . فثبت : أن المؤثر في وقوع أفعال العباد ، ليس إلا قدرة الله إما ابتداء أو بواسطة . وذلك هو المطلوب . وهذا أيضاً برهان شريف المطلوب . إلا أن البرهان المبني على اعتبار أحوال المتناقضين أشرف من هذا البرهان . وذلك لأنا في هذا البرهان نفتقر لإقامة الدلالة على كونه تعالى عالم بجميع المعلومات . حتى يثبت لنا عند ذلك : أنه تعالى كان عالماً بأفعال العباد قبل وقوعها . وهذه المقدمة إن أخذناها على سبيل أن الخصم شاهد عليها ، كان هذا الكلام الزاما برهانياً . فإن حاولنا إثباتها بالدليل ، تعذر ذلك علينا . لأن المعتمد في إثبات أنه تعالى عالم بأفعال العباد قبل وقوعها : هو أنه تعالى مقدر لها وخالق لها . فوجب أن يكون عالماً بها . فنحن إنما أثبتنا كونه تعالى عالماً بها قبل وقوعها ، لأنه ثبت كونه تعالى
The Seventh Proof. Human actions are known to God as occurring or as not occurring. And everything known to occur is necessary to occur. And everything known not to occur is necessary not to occur. And all that has been previously established. So we say: When the matter is thus, then that necessity must be either because God preferred their existence over their non-existence, or because God created what necessitates their occurrence, either directly or without an intermediary. And according to all these estimations, our goal is attained. And that which indicates the soundness of this premise is: Since the servant's action is necessary to occur at that specific time, then either its necessity is due to itself—and that is impossible, because the possible in itself is not necessary in itself—or its necessity is due to something else, and that something else is either the servant or God. The first is false, because the action which God knows will occur at such-and-such a time is judged in pre-eternity as being necessary to occur at that time, so it continues. Thus, the necessity according to this interpretation is realized in pre-eternity, but that which is not realized in pre-eternity is impossible. When this is invalidated, it is established that the effective agent in bringing about the necessity according to the interpretation we have mentioned is an attribute of God. That attribute is either knowledge or something else. The first is false, because knowledge relates to the known as it is, and it follows the known and does not cause it. So it is impossible that the cause of this necessity is God's knowledge. So it is established that the cause of this necessity is an attribute of God that directly tilts one of the two sides of the possible over the other, and that attribute is only power or will. So it is established that the effective agent in the occurrence of human actions is only God's power, either directly or through an intermediary. And that is what is sought. This also is a noble proof of what is sought. However, the proof based on considering the states of two contradictories is more noble than this proof. That is because in this proof we need to establish the evidence that God is knowledgeable of all things, so that we may thereby prove that He was knowledgeable of human actions before their occurrence. If we take this premise as a concession from the opponent, then this statement becomes a dialectical refutation. But if we attempt to prove it by evidence, that becomes difficult for us, because the basis for proving that God is knowledgeable of human actions before their occurrence is that He is their predeterminer and creator; so He must be knowledgeable of them. Thus, we only prove that He is knowledgeable of them before their occurrence because it is established that He is
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof (البرهان السابع) for the predestination of human actions. The author begins by stating a premise: God knows all human actions as either occurring or not occurring. Whatever He knows to occur is necessary to occur, and whatever He knows not to occur is necessary not to occur. This necessity must have a cause. The author then argues that this cause is either God's preference (ارجح? رجع likely means رجح) or His creation of what necessitates the action. The proof then proceeds by examining the nature of the action's necessity: it cannot be necessary by itself (because it is possible), nor can it be necessary by the servant (because the necessity is eternal, predating the servant). Thus, the necessity must come from an attribute of God. The author then eliminates knowledge as the cause, because knowledge follows the known and does not cause it. Therefore, the cause must be either power (القدرة) or will (الإرادة). The conclusion is that God's power is the effective agent in causing human actions, directly or through intermediaries. The author then evaluates this proof compared to another (the proof based on contradictory states), noting that this proof requires first establishing God's knowledge of future actions, which itself depends on His being the creator and predeterminer. If the opponent concedes this knowledge, the proof works as a dialectical argument; otherwise, it is difficult to prove independently. This shows the author's methodological awareness.

Key Terms
المقتضي
القدرة
الإرادة
ترجيح أحد طرفي الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's knowledge directly causes actions.
Correction: The author argues knowledge follows the known and does not cause; the cause is power or will.

Checkpoint
Why can the servant not be the cause of the action's necessity?
A) Because the servant is not powerful enough
B) Because the necessity is eternal and the servant is temporal
C) Because the servant's will is free
D) Because the action is known by God

Key Takeaway
The necessity of human actions originates from God's power or will, not from the action itself, the servant, or God's knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every action you take is ultimately caused by God's power—not your own independent will—how would your sense of humility and reliance on God change? Would you still feel proud of your achievements?
?
This lesson claims that the necessity of your actions is not from you, but from God's attribute. Are you ready to surrender the illusion of self-causation and acknowledge that God's power is the only effective agent? What would it mean for your dua and repentance if you accept that even your choices are decreed and enacted by God?
?
Challenge your ego: Can you sincerely thank God for both your good deeds and your mistakes, knowing He is the ultimate cause? If you believe your actions are not truly yours, does that change how you view accountability and your need for His mercy?

Methodological Note: The Proof's Dependence on Divine Knowledge
Methodological critique of the proof's reliance on divine knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's critique of this proof: it requires establishing God's knowledge of future actions, which itself depends on His being the creator.

Core Idea
This proof is dialectical; it works if the opponent concedes God's knowledge.

After concluding the proof, the author offers a methodological reflection. He notes that this proof is less noble than another proof because it relies on the premise that God knows future actions. If the opponent agrees to that premise, the proof is a valid dialectical argument. But if one tries to prove that premise independently, it becomes circular because God's knowledge of future actions is deduced from His being the creator.

Guided Path
1
Understand the author's comparison
The author compares this proof to one based on contradictory states (أحوال المتناقضين), saying the latter is nobler.
2
Identify the prerequisite: God's knowledge of future actions
This proof requires first establishing that God knows all human actions before they occur.
The author says 'we need to establish that God is knowledgeable of all things'.
3
Grasp the dialectical nature
If the opponent concedes God's knowledge, the proof works as a dialectical argument. Otherwise, proving it independently is difficult because the standard proof of God's knowledge is that He is the creator.
The passage is cut off, but the point is that the proof's strength depends on a conceded premise.

The argument that human action without a sufficient cause leads to compulsion
Two divisions showing indeterminacy leads to pure compulsion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the two divisions of this argument demonstrate that any alternative to the Ash'ari position on human action leads to compulsion (jabr).

Core Idea
Without a sufficient cause, human action collapses into pure compulsion.

This passage presents a rigorous two-part argument that challenges any view denying that a sufficient cause necessitates action. The author shows that if the act's occurrence is not determined by a condition added by the servant, it becomes mere coincidence, which is a form of compulsion. The alternative—that an additional condition is needed—leads either to an infinite regress or to the necessity of the act, both of which imply compulsion. Understanding this argument is key to grasping the Ash'ari position on causality and human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once slowly, then the translation. Note the two main divisions (qism) introduced by the author.
The passage is dense; it may help to break it into sections.
2
Identify the first division
The first scenario: the act sometimes occurs, sometimes not, without any distinguishing factor from the servant. What is the conclusion? The act becomes pure coincidence, which the author calls 'pure compulsion'.
Coincidence here means no real agency—thus jabr.
3
Trace the second division
The second scenario: the servant and conditions are insufficient, so something else must be added. Follow the two sub-branches: if the added thing is the servant's act (impossible infinite regress) or God's act (then act is either necessary or the division repeats).
The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that when all necessary conditions for influence (mu'thiriyya) are present, the act necessarily occurs; when any condition is missing, the act is impossible. This entails jabr.
5
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why does this argument matter for the debate on free will and predestination? How does it support the Ash'ari view?
The argument is internal to kalam, showing that the alternative position collapses into compulsion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل يجوز أن يحصل الفعل تارة ، وأن لا يحصل أخرى ، ولم يكن تميز حصول الفعل عن لا حصوله بأمر آخر يضمه العبد إلى المجموع الذي كان حاصلا . فحينئذ يكون حصول الفعل محض الاتفاق . وهذا أيضاً محض الجبر وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يقال : ذات العبد مع مجموع تلك الأمور غير كاف في كونها مصدراً لذلك الفعل . فحينئذ لا بد من ضم شيء آخر إليه ، وذلك الأمر الآخر إن كان فعلا له فهو محال وإلا لزم أن يحصل فعل قبل حصول أول الأفعال وذلك محال وإن لم يكن فعلاً له بل كان فعلا الله تعالى فعند حصوله قد تم كل ما لا بد منه في كونه مصدراً لأفعاله فإما أن يكون صدور أفعاله عنه واجباً أو لا يكون وحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور بعينه فثبت أن حصول الفعل عند حصول كل ما لا بد منه في المؤثرية واجب وثبت أن عند فقدان كل تلك الأمور وعند فقدان بعضها يكون صدور الفعل عن العبد ممتنعاً وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه يكون القول بالجبر لازماً وبالله التوفيق
Rather, it is possible that the act occurs sometimes and does not occur other times, and the distinction between the occurrence of the act and its non-occurrence was not due to another matter that the servant adds to the totality that was already present. Then the occurrence of the act is pure coincidence. And this also is pure compulsion (jabr). As for the second division: that it is said: the essence of the servant together with the totality of those matters is insufficient for it to be the source of that act. Then there must be an addition of something else to it, and that other thing, if it is an act of his, it is impossible, otherwise it would necessitate that an act occur before the occurrence of the first of acts, and that is impossible. And if it is not an act of his, but rather an act of God Almighty, then upon its occurrence everything necessary for him to be a source of his acts has been completed. Then either the emanation of his acts from him is necessary or it is not, and then the aforementioned division returns exactly. So it is established that the occurrence of the act upon the attainment of everything necessary for influence (al-mu'thiriyya) is necessary, and it is established that when all those matters are absent, and when some of them are absent, the emanation of the act from the servant is impossible. And on this estimation, then the statement of compulsion (al-jabr) becomes necessary. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents a two-part argument to demonstrate that any alternative to the Ash'ari position on human action leads to compulsion (jabr). The first division: if the act's occurrence is not distinguished from its non-occurrence by something the servant adds to the already present conditions, then the act's occurrence is pure chance, which is equivalent to compulsion because the agent has no real control. The second division: if the servant's essence and the conditions are insufficient, then something else must be added. If that something is the servant's own act, an infinite regress follows (an act before the first act). If it is God's act, then once it is present, all conditions for the servant to be a source of acts are complete; then either the act's emanation is necessary or not. If necessary, it is compulsion; if not, the same division recurs. Thus the conclusion is that when all necessary conditions for influence are present, the act necessarily occurs, and when any condition is lacking, the act is impossible. This entails compulsion (jabr).

Key Terms
الجبر (jabr)
الاتفاق (coincidence)
المؤثرية (influence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human actions can occur without any sufficient cause.
Correction: The argument shows that if an action occurs without a sufficient cause, it is pure coincidence, which is a form of compulsion, not genuine freedom.

Checkpoint
What does the passage conclude about the occurrence of an act when all necessary conditions for influence are present?
A) It is possible but not necessary.
B) It is necessary.
C) It is impossible.
D) It depends on the servant's choice.

Key Takeaway
When all necessary conditions for influence are present, the act necessarily occurs; otherwise it is impossible, making compulsion inevitable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed your good deeds entirely to your own will, forgetting that Allah created every condition that made that act possible? How can you begin to acknowledge His role in every action you do?
?
When you sin, do you excuse yourself by saying 'I couldn't help it' or 'it just happened'? In light of this passage, does that excuse truly absolve you, or does it reveal a deeper lack of reliance on Allah's guidance?
?
If every act is ultimately compelled by Allah's decree, how does that change the way you should think about your own responsibility? Will you use this knowledge to increase your dependence on Him or to justify your shortcomings?

10 min
Refutation of Objections: God's Power Over Servant's Actions
Refutation of ten objections and proof of God's power over the servant's action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Matalib refutes the ten objections raised by the Mu'tazila and establishes that God's power necessarily extends to the servant's actions.

Core Idea
The ten objections only bind the Mu'tazila; God's power covers all objects of power.

In this passage, the author concludes a critical argument about divine power. He addresses the ten objections previously raised against the Mu'tazila, showing they do not affect his own position. Then he constructs a proof that God's power must attach to the servant's action, based on the principle of likeness and the impossibility of preponderance without a determiner.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the structure: first a conclusion from a prior argument, then dismissal of objections, then a new proof.
The passage is logically dense.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two parts: the response to the ten objections and the constructive proof of God's power. Find where the shift occurs.
The shift is after 'لم يلزم علينا تلك النقوض'.
3
Understand the objection dismissal
The author says the ten objections only apply to Mu'tazilite positions. Since Ash'aris do not hold those, the objections are irrelevant. Why is this a valid defense?
This is a classic Ash'ari move.
4
Follow the proof logic
The proof moves from: (1) the servant's action is like God's object of power, (2) what is valid for one is valid for its like, (3) so it is valid for God's power, (4) if valid, God's power must attach, otherwise preponderance without determiner, (5) so God is powerful over it.
This is a modal argument.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that God is powerful over all objects of power, including the servant's action. How does this relate to the broader discussion of qadar?
It affirms divine omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لافتقر إلى معين آخر. ولزم التسلسل ، وهو محال . والقيد العدمي لا دخل له في التأثير. ولما سقط التعين ، لم يبق إلا أصل الماهية : وحينئذ يحصل التقريب . وأما النقوض العشرة التي أوردناها في هذه المقدمة على المعتزلة . فهي لازمة على مذاهبهم . وأما نحن إذ كنا لا نقول بتلك المذاهب ، لم يلزم علينا تلك النقوض . فثبت : أن مثل مقدور العبد مقدور الله تعالى ، وثبت : أن ما صح على الشيء ، صح على مثله ، فوجب القطع بأن مقدور العبد ، يصح أن يكون [مقدور] الله تعالى وإذا حصلت هذه الصلاحية ، وجب تعلق قدرة الله تعالى به. إذ لو لم تتعلق قدرة الله تعالى به ، مع أنه يصح [تعلق] قدرته به ، لكان تعلق قدرته ببعض المقدورات دون البعض : ترجيحاً لأحد طرفي الجانب على الآخر . وذلك لا يحصل إلا لمخصص قادر . فيلزم : أن لا الله تعالى قادراً على مقدوراته، إلا لأجل أن شيئاً آخر قدر عليه . ولما كان ذلك في حق الله تعالى محالاً ، علمنا : أنه قادر على جميع المقدورات ، فوجب القطع بكونه تعالى قادرا على مقدور العبد.
It would not need another determiner. And infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. The privative restriction has no effect in causation. When determination fell away, nothing remained except the essence of the quiddity, and then approximation occurs. As for the ten objections we raised in this introduction against the Mu'tazila, they are necessary according to their doctrines. But as for us, since we do not hold those doctrines, those objections do not follow against us. So it is established: that the like of the servant's object of power is an object of power of God Most High, and it is established: that whatever is valid for a thing is valid for its like. Thus it is necessary to decide that the servant's object of power is valid to be an object of power of God Most High. And when this validity obtains, it is necessary for the power of God Most High to be attached to it. For if the power of God Most High were not attached to it, while it is valid for His power to be attached to it, then His power being attached to some objects of power to the exclusion of others would be a preponderance of one side over the other. And that does not occur except through a powerful determiner. So it would follow that God Most High is not powerful over His objects of power except because something else determined it. And since that is impossible with respect to God Most High, we know that He is powerful over all objects of power, so it is necessary to decide that He Most High is powerful over the servant's object of power.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of objections and a constructive proof. It begins by concluding a prior argument: if determination is removed, only the essence (mahiya) remains, leading to approximation. Then it addresses ten objections raised earlier against the Mu'tazila. The author states that those objections only apply to the Mu'tazila's doctrines, not to his own school (Ash'ari). Because his school does not hold those problematic doctrines, the objections do not apply. From this, he establishes two principles: the servant's object of power is like an object of power of God, and what is valid for one thing is valid for its like. Therefore, the servant's action is valid to be an object of God's power. Once this validity is established, God's power must be attached to it. Otherwise, if God's power were not attached despite validity, that would imply a preponderance without a determiner, which is impossible. Hence God must be powerful over all objects of power, including the servant's action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly believe that God had power over your action? If so, how does this affect your understanding of your own responsibility and repentance? Today, ask yourself: Am I using God's omnipotence as an excuse to blame Him, or as a reason to seek His forgiveness and change?
?
The argument shows that denying God's power over your actions would imply a deficiency in God. Is there any area of your life where you act as if God is not in control—where you worry, scheme, or despair as if the outcome depends entirely on you? What would it mean for you to fully submit to His power in that area starting today?

Proof of Man's Ignorance of Action Details
Three-part proof of human ignorance of action details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three-part proof that a human being is ignorant of the detailed components of his own voluntary actions.

Core Idea
You never know the full details of your own actions.

This passage from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents a rational proof that a person is unaware of the minutiae of his own voluntary movements. The proof examines three dimensions: the physical parts of the body, the spaces traversed, and the instants of time. By reflecting on our everyday experience, we can see that our ignorance is complete in all three respects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
The passage uses a repetitive structure: 'Also... also...' for each part.
2
Identify the three dimensions of ignorance
The proof presents three areas where a mover lacks knowledge: the number of body parts, the number of spaces traversed, and the number of time instants. Find each in the text.
3
Notice the term 'by necessity' (bi-al-darura)
The author claims we know by necessity that the mover is unaware. Reflect on why this is considered self-evident.
This is a key epistemological claim in kalam.
4
Understand how the conclusion is drawn
After presenting all three parts, the author concludes that the servant is absolutely unaware of the details of his actions. See how each part contributes.
5
Consider the theological implication
This proof is used in discussions of qadar (divine decree). Reflect on how human ignorance of action details affects the debate on free will and divine control.
The proof does not deny that the action occurs, only that the agent knows its details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجزاء كثيرة موجودة بالفعل . أما عند من يثبت الجوهر الفرد ، فلا شك فيه . وأما عند من ينكره ، فلا شك أنه معترف بأن مجموع البدن ، مؤلف من الأعضاء البسيطة - أعني العظام والغضاريف والأعصاب والعضلات والرباطات ، إلى غير ذلك من الأعضاء البسيطة - فإذا حرك الانسان بدنه ، فلا معني لهذا التحريك إلا أنه حرك مجموع تلك الأجزاء ، لكنا نعلم بالضرورة أنه البتة غير عالم بأعداد تلك الأعضاء. وأيضاً : فلا شك أنه لما حرك بدنه ، فقد نقل تلك الجثة من حيز إلى حيز ، ومر بما بين الطرفين ، مع أنه غير عالم بأعداد تلك الأحياز فلا يمكنه أن يعلم ما بين مبدأ تلك الحركة إلى منتهاها . وأيضاً : فلا شك أن تلك الحركة وقعت في مقدار معين من الزمان، وذلك القدر المعين من الزمان ، مركب من آنات متتالية متعاقبة. وهو البتة لا يعلم مقدار الزمان ، ولا عدد الآنات ، التي منها تركب ذلك الزمان . فثبت بما ذكرنا : أن من انتقل من مكان إلى مكان ، فهو لم يعلم أن الأجزاء التي حركها . كم هي ؟ والأحياز التي منها تألفت تلك المسافة التي فيها وقعت الحركة . كم هي ؟ والآنات التي منها تألف الزمان ، الذي هو طرف لتلك الحركة. كم هي فثبت : أن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعاله البتة.
From many parts already existing. As for he who affirms the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard), there is no doubt about it. And as for he who denies it, there is no doubt that he acknowledges that the sum total of the body is composed of simple organs – I mean bones, cartilages, nerves, muscles, and ligaments, up to other simple organs. So when a man moves his body, there is no meaning to this movement except that he moves the totality of those parts, but we know by necessity (bi-al-darura) that he is absolutely unaware of the numbers of those organs. Also: there is no doubt that when he moved his body, he transferred that mass from one space (hayyiz) to another, and passed through what is between the two extremes, while he is unaware of the numbers of those spaces, so he cannot know what is between the beginning of that movement and its end. Also: there is no doubt that that movement occurred in a specified amount of time, and that specified amount of time is composed of successive consecutive instants (anāt). And he is absolutely unaware of the amount of time, nor the number of instants from which that time is composed. So it is established by what we have mentioned: that whoever moves from one place to another, he does not know how many the parts he moved are, nor how many the spaces that composed that distance in which the movement occurred are, nor how many the instants that composed the time, which is the extent of that movement, are. So it is established: that the servant (al-‘abd) is absolutely unaware of the details of his actions.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a proof that a human being is ignorant of the detailed components of his own voluntary actions. The author presents a three-part argument, each part building on the previous. First, he considers the composition of the body. Whether one accepts the atomic theory (al-jawhar al-fard) or not, everyone agrees the body is composed of many simple parts (bones, cartilages, etc.). When a person moves his body, he moves the whole collection, but he does not know the exact number of those parts. Second, the author considers the spatial dimension. When the body moves, it traverses a distance composed of many individual spaces (ahiyaz). The mover is unaware of the number of these spaces, yet the movement occurs through them. Third, the author considers the temporal dimension. The movement takes a specific amount of time, which is composed of consecutive instants (anāt). The mover does not know the number of instants. From these three considerations, the author concludes that a person who moves from one place to another does not know the number of parts he moved, the number of spaces traversed, or the number of instants elapsed. Hence, the servant (al-‘abd) is absolutely unaware of the details of his actions. This proof is used in kalam to argue that human actions are not fully known to the agent, thus challenging the notion of complete human control over actions.

Key Terms
جوهر فرد
حيّز
آنات
الضرورة
